The hallway suddenly feels smaller, constrictive. Like the walls are closing in on her, threatening to crush her. 

“Rio,” Agatha’s voice cracks, almost whiny now, raw with desperation. She folds forward on the wall, shoulders slumping as her arms hold her stomach like she can’t physically stand anymore. “Please, my love…”

The words stop Rio in her tracks. Pain sears through her like she touched a live wire. She wants to reach for her, to grab her. She wants this to be a false reality, a mirror of a real universe where they are together, happy, without these strings attached. 

In that moment, another realization hits her. The puppet master in all of this. The real cause of her pain. 

Evanora. 

“So that’s it huh? You are going to let her control you. Dictate your life?” Rio’s voice shakes with a mixture of anger and grief. She’s waiting, longing for Agatha to contradict her; to tell her it’s not true. She doesn’t want to know the truth. She wants a different ending. 

“I don’t have a choice,” Agatha whispers, barely audible, the finality of it cutting Rio’s chest in two. 

“Seems I’m not the only one concerned about her job,” Rio rolls her eyes. 

“That’s not fair.”

“So you are going to spend your entire life in a fake marriage that you don’t want? Being unhappy?” Rio’s voice drips with accusation, disbelief and under it all - pain. 

“We can’t always get what we want,” Agatha murmurs, her voice steady but the words hollow. “Sometimes we are just dealing with the cards we are dealt.”

“This doesn’t even sound like you,” Rio steps closer, her index finger hooking under Agatha’s chin, forcing her to look up at her. “Is that a line that mommy fed you?” 

“Fuck you!” Agatha jerks back, yanking her chin free. “I’m not doing this.” She shoves past Rio, shoulder colliding into her. “Aren’t you supposed to be my attending? Helping me in my professional career? Where does lesbian life advice play into that?” Agatha spits the words like venom.

“Then I’m an idiot for thinking I was more than that,” Rio retaliates. 

The sudden ping of elevator doors opening breaks through the tension. Two hotel security officers step out, scanning the hallway. 

“Excuse me,” one of them says, an older man in a stretched polo, pot belly stretching the fabric. He looks out of breath, despite taking an elevator ride to reach them. “We received reports of a disturbance.” 

Rio straightens, falling into a professional mode instantly. She flashes a toothy, polite smile even though every fiber of her body is still humming with tension. “We were just leaving,” she says smoothly. 

“She was just leaving,” Agatha corrects, turning down the hallway in the opposite direction. Her posture rigid with quiet defiance. 

“Agatha?” Rio calls, desperation rising quickly. “Agatha!” She calls again, but Agatha doesn’t slow, she doesn’t look back. 

Just before Agatha disappears around the threshold back to the hotel room, Rio’s frustration boils over. “You are a coward!” She yells, her words full of frustration, heartbreak and barely contained fury. 

No response awaits her. 

Rio pivots, shoulders tight, and begins to leave. She steals one last glance back at the party door. And swears she sees a flicker of movement. The back of Jen’s head, darting back inside. 

Chapter End Notes

Sorry, not sorry. I've been waiting for this chapter for so long.

Chapter 12: Longing

Chapter Notes

Trigger warning for mentions of abortion, maternal emotional and physical abuse. Tags added.

Songs for this chapter: everybody scream by florence and make this go on forever by snow patrol

See the end of the chapter for more notes

 

Rio rolls over in bed and groans, the motion sending a sharp pulse of pain through her skull. As her body stirs fully awake, memories crash into her. She’s still in her hotel room. Alone. Her hangover slams into her reminding her that after her fall out with Agatha, she went straight to the hotel bar, drowning her sorrows alone while the party continued upstairs. 

The details are a bit fuzzy. Multiple glasses of tequila, an embarrassing amount of tears and endless glances at her phone, begging it to buzz. 

At least she remembers she was alone. Right now, she doesn’t know if that makes her feel better or worse. 

Agatha’s strap still sits discarded on the floor of her hotel room. She didn’t even bother to wash it. For a moment, Rio thinks about throwing it away, but she won’t leave that horror for the housekeepers to find. 

Dragging herself upright, she stumbles to the bathroom. The light is blinding, worsening her headache and the sudden motion leaves her stomach revolting. She heaves into the toilet until her throat is raw. 

The shower that follows is brutally hot but it does nothing to strip away the memory of Agatha. Her body aches with it - the purple bruises along her hips where her fingers clamped tight, the soreness between her thighs. She hates it. Hates that her body remembers what her mind is screaming to forget. 

She shoves on a pair of sunglasses as she grabs her bag to leave, hoping anyone who sees her is also too hung over to recognize her.

As she climbs into the elevator, mercifully, it’s empty. She slouches into the back corner. 

It lowers two floors before it stops, the doors opening on the third floor. 

Jen walks in. Eyes down. Rio pretends not to notice she’s wearing the same clothes from last night. 

“Rio,” she greets her, her voice a combination of pity and warning. “Do you want to talk about it? I mean, I can’t say I didn’t warn you but…”

“Just stop, Jen.”

“I’m just saying, I think that…”

Rio cuts her off again. “Oh yes, please tell me all about sleeping with an intern! That must be fascinating coming from you; or did you not just leave Alice’s bed?” 

Jen freezes, eyes wide. “What? How did you..?”

“You got in at the third floor,” Rio spits. “Where the residents were staying.” Rio looks her up and down. “And same clothes.” 

Color rushes to Jen’s cheeks. “Fuck, I wasn’t very sly, was I?” 

“Didn’t even last a day.” Rio folds her arms. “So no, I don’t need your pity today.”

Her words are meant to harm. And they do. 

The rest of the elevator ride is silent. 

—

By the next morning, Rio wants to call in sick. Again. 

Her body is practically begging for it. She tells herself it’s a prolonged hangover. A two day age-related punishment. But she knows better. This isn’t her body. It’s her mind. Emotional whiplash. The fallout of crashing out over someone half her age. 

Calling out would feel like surrendering to those feelings. Like letting Agatha win.

No. 

Today she’ll walk into that hospital polished and professional. Every ounce of her will scream control. 

The thoughts jolt her with deja vu. The same mentality when she first slept with Agatha. Convincing herself she could compartmentalize. 

Except this time, it’s not because of a slip up.  

It’s because everything’s changed. 

For those two days, the fight runs like a film reel that Rio can’t turn off. Every word. Every pause. Every movement of Agatha’s mouth. She drags the memories through her mind until they’re raw and frayed. 

Agatha telling her she won’t leave him. 

Rio spitting back that she’s a coward. And God, that one even cuts her, jagged and unhealed. 

Then the silence. And the leaving. 

Cold and empty. 

One thing sticks, stubborn and impossible to shake. 

Please, my love.

My love.

Love. 

The words dig in, relentless. Not a mistake, right? Something Agatha tossed out casually or was it really Agatha’s true feelings slipping through in a moment of desperation?

Rio tells herself it doesn’t matter. Love means nothing if the path of Agatha’s life has already been carved in stone. And yet - the thought presses on her chest, heavy and immoveable. 

She fights to try to sleep that night - tossing and turning until she finally falls asleep and dreams only of her. By morning, she feels hollowed out, starting in on the caffeine intake before her alarm even rings.

She hauls the door to the conference room open, loud and aggressive. 

Billy and Alice’s eyes dart up, flinching as if ready to shield themselves from the impending battle.

But Agatha doesn’t even look up. 

It’s deliberate, calculated. Agatha spends the morning breezing past her in the conference room without a glance, snatching her patient list without a word. 

And when she finally is forced to speak, it’s with a clipped, dismissive tone she would use with a stranger. Not someone she shared a bed with only days ago. Underneath the chill of Agatha’s gaze, Rio still wants to feel the heat of what they once were. But that seems impossibly far away now. 

Morning rounds are eerily silent except for the sounds of clicking keyboards and the scratching of pens. 

Rio struggles to concentrate on her computer, lab numbers blur, sentences repeat and dissolve on her screen. She’s chosen her seat at the conference room table with precision - close enough to study Agatha, to catch the smallest flickers of her expressions. Every furrow of her brow, every upturn of her lip. 

And she hates it. 

A little part of her hates that in only a few months, Agatha turned her world upside down. Made her question everything she knew, stripped her of certainty - made her want to crawl on her hands and knees to get to her. 

She hates that she can’t have her - not in the way she wants her. Wholly. Unrestrained. Free. 

She hates how much she might love…

No. She can’t think that. Not here. Not now. Maybe not ever. 

The only thing that became wildly clear during that resident retreat weekend, was that Agatha will choose him. And her mother. Over Rio. 

That is something she is still grappling with as she cues up the next patient for rounds. 

“This patient admitted last night for an MI needs to be optimized on medical therapy. Who can tell me what needs to be added to his regimen?” Rio forces herself to switch her focus back on work, even if her gaze lingers on Agatha a second too long. 

The room is silent again.

“Agatha?” Rio probes, even though it’s not her patient. Or her turn to answer.

“Ask cardiology,” Agatha says flippantly.

“I’m sure they know the answer, but we are here for your education,” Rio snaps. 

“Fine.” Agatha grates. “He’s already on a statin, but it needs to be high dose. And we will add a beta blocker, ace-inhibitor and aspirin.” 

“Now was that so hard?” Rio’s words spit sarcasm.

The look Agatha gives her could kill. “Am I done? I’d like to go back to charting.” 

“No, you aren’t. There is a patient in the emergency room that we need to admit.”

“Sounds like Alice can do it,” Agatha snaps in deliberate defiance. 

“You are doing it.” Rio doesn’t leave room for argument, but Agatha does anyway. 

“And if I don’t?” She challenges. 

“I put on your evaluation that I recommend you fail the rotation.”

She hears Alice gasp. 

Agatha slams her hands down on the table as she shoves her chair back, the scrape loud. She stalks toward the door, shoulders stiff. 

“Don’t be too dramatic or anything,” Rio taunts as she follows her out the door.

The emergency room is filled with the usual buzz of elderly patients dozing under fluorescent lights, a drunk man shouting for a turkey sandwich and the sharp smell of antiseptic mixing with old, stale coffee. 

Rio lets Agatha sign into the workstation, giving her space to click through the chart before she sinks down into the chair next to her, angling just so that her thigh grazes hers. Usually, the touch would earn her a quick quip, a sly sideways glance, or a promise of later. 

This time, Agatha simply moves away. “Don’t,” she breathes. But she doesn’t sound angry, just…sad. 

Rio bites her lip and scoots away, leaving a strip of cold space between them. They dissolve into silence, the sounds of the emergency room chaos constantly swirling around them. 

Rio’s leg bounces beneath the work station table, a restless pulse of energy. Her fingernail taps on the mouse; a relentless sharp clicking noise cutting through their silence. 

“Can you stop?” Agatha suddenly snaps, glaring at her. 

“I’m not doing anything.”

“Yes, you are. You are fidgeting and I’m trying to concentrate.” 

Rio picks up a pen instead, her thumb pressing the plunger up and down endlessly. She flips it a few times in her fingers, until it slips, flying sideways to land next to her. 

“For fucks sake!” Agatha practically yells. 

“So that’s what it takes for you to talk to me?” Rio lifts an eyebrow as she picks up the pen from its spot on Agatha’s keyboard. “Good to know.”

“What do you want from me, Rio?” 

“I want you to talk to me.”

“You mentioned that. But you ask me questions you don’t want the answers to then get mad when I tell the truth.” 

Rio’s voice drops to a low whisper. “You called me your love.”

Agatha freezes, her eyes widening silently. Then she stiffens her jaw. “You heard that.”

“Do you want to take it back?”

“It doesn’t matter. It can’t…”

“It matters to me,” Rio’s voice breaks slightly. 

“Rio….” Agatha says her name like a warning. “Don’t. Don’t do that. This…we were having fun. That’s it, right?”

The words feel like a dagger, twisting into her skin. As much as she wants to pretend there is more. This weekend showed her she was a fool. Grasping at straws of a life that can never happen. Proof she was lying to herself. 

“Can we focus on the patient now?” Agatha pleads. “Please?”

“Yeah…” the words come out small. “Yeah, we can.”

Then Rio leans forward, squinting at the patient’s chart on the screen. A 21-year old female here for abdominal pain found to have suspected ectopic pregnancy. 

Then at the bottom of the chart: mother at bedside, refusing intervention.

Fuck.

The universe is laughing at her. 

—

“Agatha, what’s your plan?” She asks as they finish reviewing the patient. 

The tension sits just below the surface, a volcano ready to erupt. But God dammit, one thing years of medicine has taught her is how to ignore all her shit in the moment and focus on the patient. 

“We need to call OB. They can determine if she needs surgical or medical intervention,” Agatha’s tone shifts instantly into professional mode. Her back straightens as she adjusts her white coat and stands. 

“Right,” Rio rises to follow. “Let’s make sure the family understands the seriousness of the situation. There is a note that the mother is refusing treatment for her daughter.” 

A flicker of color drains from Agatha’s face. “If the pregnancy continues, the fallopian tube could rupture, causing life-threatening hemorrhage.” 

“Exactly. It’s not a matter of if, it’s when,” Rio pauses outside the door. “I’m going to let you take the lead.” 

As they step inside, a frail brunette sits in the bed, her knees drawn up to her chest. Her mother is pacing the room, phone in hand, texting furiously. 

“Finally,” the mother snaps, before they can introduce themselves. “We have been waiting forever. She feels better now; she’s ready to discharge.” 

“Ok…” Agatha falters for a breath, then steadies. “I’m Dr. Harkness. This is Dr. Vidal. I wanted to make sure you understand what’s happening with Carol.” 

“I know perfectly well,” the mother’s eyes flash up, filled with hostility, “You doctors are trying to push her into an abortion!” 

Agatha inhales sharply. “Your daughter’s pregnancy is ectopic. It is implanted in her fallopian tube. To try to save her life, the pregnancy has to be terminated.”

Rio gives Agatha a discreet nudge, in the side, urging her to focus on the patient rather than the mother. 

“Carol,” Agatha starts as she turns to the patient. “Do you understand what I’m telling you.”

The patient looks between her mother and Agatha before she gives the smallest of nods. 

But the mother cuts in again, her voice rising, “See, I knew it! That’s all these liberal types want to do is push for abortions! I bet you are going to make some vaccine with her baby’s parts!” The mother starts yelling now, her words venomous. 

Rio braces herself for Agatha to snap back - to bear her teeth and rip into the mother until Rio has to drag her from the room. Like she’s seen her do before. But she doesn’t. She just….backs down. 

“Ok. Well…umm..I guess…” Her voice falters, her words falling over themselves. “I can get discharge paperwork…”

“Damn right you will,” the mother says triumphantly. Agatha’s shoulders slump slightly, her frame seeming to curl inward. 

Rio can see the defeat on her face, the way she folds and caves under the pressure - it’s so unlike her usual. The weight of a mother’s fury pressing her down, forcing her to cave. 

Suddenly, she feels like an ass for putting her in this room, this situation. 

“Carol,” Rio steps in, her tone crips. “You are over 18. You can make your own medical decision. Technically, your mother doesn’t get to decide for you.” 

“Excuse me!” the mother snaps. “I am still her mother, despite her age!” 

“No,” comes a small voice from the hospital bed. “Mom, I know this is your religion or whatever, but it’s not mine. I’m not going to die because you don’t understand.” She pauses, watching the redness rise in her mother’s face. “I know I need to terminate.”

“We will go call OB,” Rio says definitely. She pulls Agatha gently by the shoulder, ushering her out the door. 

Out in the hallway, she closes the door just enough to create a buffer from the mother’s yelling inside. She starts walking wordlessly through the emergency room halls, out the side door and into the crisp air. 

Agatha follows silently, her shoulders tight, her hands stuffed into her white coat pockets. 

When they stop in a courtyard, the same one where Agatha faced her first patient death all those weeks ago, Rio finally turns to her.

“Hey…” Rio’s voice is careful. “That wasn’t you back there.” She keeps a measured distance, letting Agatha absorb her words. “You don’t have to cave to her. You are still the doctor in charge.” 

Agatha swallows. “I know…I just didn’t want to make her angrier." She still sounds so small. 

For a beat, they stand there, the cool evening air cutting through their white coats. Rio draws her arms around herself, trying to stay warm. 

“This isn’t about the patient anymore, is it?” Rio tests. “She’s really got a chokehold on you, doesn’t she?” She doesn’t mean the words to come out harsh, but they do. Bitter resentment toward Evanora flares in her chest. 

Agatha’s nostrils flare at her words, “She’s still my mother, Rio,” she bites back. 

“But she doesn’t have to be in charge of you,” Rio tries to keep her voice controlled but she feels herself growing angry at the situation. 

Agatha doesn’t respond, she just purses her lips. 

And Rio can’t help it, the frustration from the other night comes right back to the surface - angry and hot. “Are you really going to marry him?” 

“Do you think I have a choice?” Agatha snaps instantly. 

“Yes, you do.”

“Ha!” Agatha laughs, something bitter. “I don’t. This is so much bigger than you know. You think I can run home and tell her ‘Hey mom! Screw this engagement, I’ve been fucking my attending instead? How do you think that would go over?”

“I’m not saying to do that, Agatha!” Rio feels her voice rising. “But you can tell her no.” 

Agatha shakes her head bitterly. “I go against my mother’s wishes and she gets me kicked out of the program. And blacklisted from every residency in the country. Then what?” She spits, her cheeks flushing with anger as she balls her fists at her sides. “I’m a failed doctor. I can’t get a job or a board certification. Are you going to take me in then like some stray cat?” 

Yes, the word pulses inside Rio like a heartbeat. Instead of saying it, she steps closer, unable to stop herself despite all their fighting. Her hands frame Agatha’s face, thumbs brushing against flushed cheeks. She feels Agatha slowly soften in the grasp, her fists loosening. 

And God, the sight of those unshed tears in Agatha’s eyes nearly ruins her. 

“You are in charge of your life. You make the decisions that matter,” she tries to tell her, but Agatha instantly scoffs at her words. 

“You say that,” Agatha starts, “but it doesn’t feel like that when she’s standing over me, Rio.” 

“I know,” Rio tilts her head, like she’s helpless against the pull between them. “Just…” 

Her words fail, and fuck it, despite everything the magnetic force gets her again and she closes the distance, kissing her gently, testing. 

Agatha exhales into her mouth like a surrender, slowly melting into her like the current pulls her just as much as it does Rio. She starts pressing back, hungry. As her tongue slips into Rio’s mouth, she feels herself spiraling right back into Agatha’s gravitational pull. Her hands Agatha’s waist, finger slipping under her scrubs to brush the skin on her stomach. 

She’s thinking about rushing her toward the wall behind her, her fingers sliding into her pants to test her wetness. 

Instead, she forces herself to pull away before their public exhibition gets them both in trouble. 

Rio rests her forehead against Agatha’s as they catch their breath. 

“Go home, get some rest. I’ll finish this case,” she says as she watches Agatha lick her swollen lips. “We will start fresh tomorrow.” 

She hopes Agatha catches that she means more than just this case. That she knows she’s willing to fight for her. Day by day. 

Agatha nods as a small smile forms on her lips. “Yeah…yeah we can do that.” 

Then she heads toward the parking lot. 

—-

Rio stays too late that night - the residents have long since gone home. She should too, the resident notes needed to be signed hours ago. She just can’t seem to focus. Her brain loops every word with Agatha in the past few days. 

It feels like she is standing on train tracks. She sees the oncoming light, hears the thunder of the wheels - Agatha’s impending marriage, her mother’s grip on her life - all barreling toward her. She wants to stick out her hands to stop it. But she knows that’s impossible. So she doesn’t move, she just braces for impact. 

Rio’s pager buzzes and she grabs it, seeing the ER number. 

She frowns and calls them back. “Dr. Vidal speaking. I’m not on admissions tonight.” 

“Hold on,” the unit secretary says, ignoring her.

“Dr.Vidal!” The familiar voice of one of the long term ER attendings comes on the other line. “I’ve got a patient for you.”

“Yeah, I’m not doing the admissions tonight. Dr. Strange is.” She reaches to hang up the phone.

“Wait, wait. You are going to want to take this one.” He pauses. “She’s asking for you.”

“Okay…” Rio hesitates. She pulls out a pen and paper ready to take notes on the patient. “Go ahead, name?”

“She didn’t want me to go into detail, she just asked me to just have you come see her. Room 14.” And the line clicks dead. 

Rio doesn’t know what kind of game the emergency room is playing, but she’s a bit annoyed. She logs back onto her computer, pulling up the patient board. 

Room 14: Confidential 

Two authorizations are required before the chart will open. Rio clicks through, attempting to pull up the name. 

Jane Doe. 

Chief complaint: Multi-trauma 

Her pulse spikes a bit, unease starting to prick at her. She isn’t a trauma surgeon. This shouldn’t be her case. The best she can come up with is it’s a former patient, asking to see her again. 

Room 14 is in the corner of the ER, curtains drawn tight. It’s quiet in this corner, closed off from the usual chaos from the rest of the emergency room. 

A nurse hurries toward her. “Oh, Dr. Vidal! “I’m glad you are here. She’s been asking for you.”

“It wasn’t clear on the phone what’s going on.”

“Poor thing. She has a lung contusion, splenic laceration and three broken ribs. She has a head laceration that needs sutures too.” She glances around to make sure no one hears her. “She says it’s a car accident but that doesn’t make sense. There was no seatbelt sign, no airbag burns. Honestly, just between us, it looks like someone took a baseball bat to her…”

“I’m sorry,” Rio shakes her head trying to piece it all together. “How old did you say she was?”

“Oh I didn’t,” the nurse flips the ER paper chart open. “Umm…25.”

Rio’s heart drops. 

“I was thinking she needs to be admitted at least overnight…” the nurse starts but Rio doesn’t hear another word. 

She’s grabbing the door handle, pushing it open. 

The first thing she sees is the tubing - clear lines snaking across pale skin. A hospital gown drowns the small frame in the bed. 

A bloodstain streaks across one temple, an open laceration sits above her eyebrow. And her brown hair is tangled, splayed across the hospital pillow. 

Rio takes a step closer, further into the room.

Her chest tightens as the face comes into focus.

Her world stops.

Agatha. 

Chapter End Notes

is this canon? I might be taking a few creative liberties. We know Evanora basically hated Agatha (“I should have killed you the moment you left my body”) but I’m not sure it was always like that between the two of them. We see that Agatha was a part of her coven, so Evanora did invite her in - and that coven largely seemed like mothers and daughters based on what we know of the Salem Seven. So it does seem at some point Evanora was teaching her and despite her likely abusive nature, they did work/learn together in some capacity. Well, up until Agatha basically snapped and killed them all (but they came after her first!)

Chapter 13: Mend

Chapter Notes

thank you to @spiralslide on twt for being a sounding board for these upcoming chapter. most of the plot is all mapped out now. it's going to get crazy people. hold on tight.

 

Rio steps quietly into the room, softening her movements so as to not wake her. Agatha’s eyes are closed where she rests in the bed. Purple bruising paints the side of her cheek and a small, angry laceration lies open above her eyebrow. Her left arm wraps protectively around her ribs, every breath shallow and cautious. 

Rio reaches carefully, brushing her hand along her foot beneath the hospital blanket. 

“Hi,” Agatha’s eyes meet hers, looking far too large and scared, red rimming the outside. Her cheeks shine faintly where tears have tracked and dried. Even the edges of her nostrils are red and angry. “You came.”

Rio swallows hard, steadier her voice before she speaks. “Didn’t have much of a choice. You left it quite a mystery.”

“Seemed best to maintain some autonomy.”

Rio rounds the bed, planting herself along the side. She lowers the bedrail. Her tone drops, fear and anger swirling together. “Agatha, what the hell happened?” 

“Car accident,” she answers too quickly. 

“Bullshit. What did she do?” 

“Like I said,” Agatha breaks, like she’s on the verge of crying; her words coming out small. “Car accident.” 

And Rio can’t help it anymore. Agatha might not be hers. She may never get to be hers again. But in this moment, Agatha needs her. 

“Sweetheart…” The sentiment rushes out before she can stop it. But it still feels right. Her hand raises, hovering above Agatha’s bruised cheek. .

“Rio…” Agatha looks up at her, tears silently falling now. 

Rio slips her shoes off, lifting the blanket to slip into the spot next to her. She moves slowly and carefully, curling herself around Agatha’s trembling frame. Her arms gingerly move around to Agatha’s shoulders, careful not to move her too suddenly. 

“Someone could see you, you know,” Agatha murmurs even as her head finds Rio’s shoulder. 

“I don’t care.” Rio’s tone turns more serious. “You have to get out of there.”

“And what? Where would I go? I have an intern salary.”

“Come stay with me.”

“Then what? She fires you. And me.”

“And we run away together. I hear Alaska needs doctors.”

Agatha starts to let out a small laugh, but stops short, wincing at the motion. “I wouldn’t be a doctor, Rio. I’d be a residency drop out.”

“I’ll be your sugar mama then. You can take up fly fishing.” 

Agatha rests her head on Rio’s shoulder again, sighing. “That does sound nice.” 

They stay like that for a while, unmoving. The only noises are the faint sounds of Agatha’s blood pressure cuff inflating every few minutes and the slow drip of her IV fluids through the tubing. It’s as peaceful as it can be - for the hospital. 

At last, Rio tilts her head, murmuring into her hair. “I need to suture that head lac, you know.”

“Mmhmm,” Agatha murmurs with her eyes closed. “But you are so cozy.” 

Rio places a small kiss on her temple. “I’m sorry, I need to get to it before the edges start healing.”

She begins to slide out of bed, easing her way out as best she can without disturbing Agatha. She winces anyway. 

“Morphine?”

“Something. Please. It hurts to breathe.”

“I’ll be right back.” Rio squeezes her hand before stepping out to grab supplies and a nurse for the medication. 

She closes the curtain and the door behind her.

In the supply room, she gathers sutures, forceps, a vial of lidocaine, gauze and a small bandage. She flags down the nurse and orders morphine for Agatha. 

When she finally rounds the corner back to Agatha’s room, the door is cracked open, the curtains drawn wide. 

And standing at the threshold is Evanora. 

Even though it’s well into the evening, she’s still dressed like she’s stepping into the office wearing cream tailored pants with a black leather belt and a high turtleneck black sweater. She took the time to grab her hospital badge before leaving the house. 

Rio’s first instinct is to tackle her. Luckily the sensible side of her kicks in before she does. 

“Evanora,” Rio says, her voice flat and annoyed. 

Evanora crosses her arms, her gaze slides from Agatha back to her. “So you’re her attending.” 

Fuck, Rio’s throat dries. She flicks her eyes to Agatha, sticking her tongue in her cheek. She hopes Agatha realizes she’s silently asking how much Evanora knows. 

Agatha shakes her head softly.  

Rio squares her shoulders and moves to stand between Evanora and the bed. A physical shield for Agatha. “I’m her attending, tonight.”

Evanora’s mouth twists, an almost evil grin across her lips. “You know that’s not what I meant.” She steps closer, lowering her voice like she’s a predator about to devour her prey. “It’s curious, though. The way you always seem to be hovering. The way she looks at you. I’ve seen it before - in other residents; other…attachments.” She lets the word linger, poisonous. 

Her gaze slides deliberately back to Agatha. “Some people just can’t help themselves, parading around their sin like it’s salvation.” 

Agatha flinches, the words stinging.

“If you take her away, you don’t just lose a physician. You lose someone irreplaceable. To this hospital. To her patients.” She bites her lip, her voice so soft it’s mostly unrecognizable. “To me.”

“That’s quite the admission,” Rio hears a female voice from the committee cuts in, the words slicing the moment apart. 

She blinks a few times, the room coming back into focus. 

Agatha coughs then, tilting her chin up and straightening her shoulders like she’s resetting herself.  “She’s just a good doctor, that’s all,” She shrugs like she said nothing of importance. 

But the words burn in Rio’s chest, warm and steady. Agatha defended her, claimed her. Risked her job for her just as much as Rio did. 

Finally, the committee dismisses Lilia and Rio, stating they will talk and email her with a final decision.

Rio feels hollow. Exhaustion presses behind her eyes, frustration sitting heavy in her chest. Her interns shouldn’t have been subjected to this shit. But at the same time, she feels like it must be worth it - for her. For Agatha. 

They are halfway down the corridor when a voice calls out behind them. 

“Hold on,” Hela yells down the hall. “We need to speak with you.”

Rio’s stomach drops. No committee reaches a verdict that fast. Not unless it’s bad. 

They don’t even have Rio sit again when she enters the room. She just stands at the doorway awkwardly, her hand clutched around the phone in her hand. 

“We’ve agreed there is not enough evidence that Dr. Vidal demonstrated any professional misconduct that night,” Hela states, her tone professional. 

Tony sits slouched in his chair, his eyes glued to his phone screen. He looks indifferent, angry - likely outvoted in the decision. 

“Apart from Evanora’s word, no one else saw anything out of sorts,” Hela continues. “Nothing in her records, past conduct or evaluations suggest a pattern of behavior that warrants suspension.” 

Rio lets out a shaky sigh. 

They won. They actually won. 

Lilia places her hand on her forearm, a quiet congratulations between them.

“With that said,” she continues, “there are some concerns about the nature of Dr. Vidal’s relationships with residents that may be pushing the lines of professionalism.” 

The relief is short lived. 

Across the table, Tony looks up for the first time. His lips curl into a small, smug smile. He raises his eyebrow like he’s satisfied with the small victory. 

“At this time, we elect Dr. Vidal not continue to have residents under her care,” Hela concludes. 

Fuck. 

“She can resume work immediately. Independently.” Then she gathers her papers, leaving no room for questions. 

The committee shuffles out of the room, murmuring between each other. As Tony passes her, his shoulder bumps her, deliberate and malicious. “Oops,” he murmurs in a mocking tone. 

Rio feels stiff, rooted in the place where they left her. The victory feels thin, almost false. They gave her what they could, and stripped away everything else.

For a moment, she just stands there, Lilia beside her, quiet, waiting for her to move. Then something inside her steadies and she reaches a resolve. 

Evanora will keep trying to take her down piece by piece. To take them down. So she’s going to reclaim her power with something she can’t touch, something that she is sure is still hers alone. 

— 

“So?” Agatha runs to meet her in the hallway, but she keeps her voice low. 

“I got my job back,” Rio manages a tired smile. 

Agatha looks at her excitedly, ready to wrap her arms around Rio in a hug. She spots Lilia at her side and quickly drops her arms, opting for a nod instead. 

Lilia’s eyes narrow at the exchange. Then she turns to Rio, “I’ll call you,” she says before turning away to leave them. 

Rio hovers her hand over Agatha’s lower back as soon as Lilia turns away. “Hey,” she softens her voice. “Let’s walk.” 

Rio starts leading Agatha toward the back of the hospital, into the stairwell. As soon as the door clicks shut, Agatha wraps her arms around Rio. She plants a quick kiss on her lips.

“We did it!” she grins, pulling back just enough to search Rio’s face. But Rio’s smile doesn’t stay.

“Agatha…” she starts. 

“Oh no,” Agatha interrupts, groaning. “I know that tone. What’s wrong? Why aren’t you more happy about this?”

“It’s good. Don’t get me wrong,” Rio starts carefully. “They let me have my job back. But…” She hesitates. “That’s it. They won’t let me supervise residents anymore. They’re concerned I’ve crossed boundaries.”

“Wait, no. I didn’t mean anything, I swear…” She starts to pull backward out of Rio’s arms. 

Rio tightens her grip on her waist. “Agatha.” 

“Okay, maybe not nothing, but nothing obvious.”

Rio sighs. “Billy was worse.”

Her eyes widen. “Then they can’t do this! It’s not right. We should…”

“Agatha.” Rio says again, her voice softening. “You have to be a doctor on your own too. You’ll still have an attending. It just won’t be me.”

“But..” Her eyes meet Rio’s. “I need you.”

“No, you don’t.” Rio brushes a thumb along her cheek. “You can do this without me. I’ll still be here, just… not over your shoulder.”

Agatha frowns. “Then how am I supposed to sneak around with you if I hardly get to see you?” She adds a slight pout to her expression.

“That’s actually what I wanted to talk to you about.”

“How to still have sex in the hospital?”

Rio laughs quietly. “No. I was thinking… maybe we wouldn’t have to sneak around the hospital at all.”

Agatha blinks, uncertain. “Okay?”

“You’ve been staying with me for a week,” Rio says. “But what’s your long-term plan?”

“I, uh…” Agatha shifts, biting her lip. She looks slightly embarrassed. “I hadn’t really thought about it. I don’t want to go back to my mother’s. I think she cut off my cards anyway. They stopped working the day after my ‘accident.’ I could get my own place, or maybe Billy needs a roommate, but he’s sooo messy…” 

“Agatha.” Rio catches her rambling, fingertips tilting her chin up. “Hey. Look at me.”

Agatha stills.

“I’m asking you to move in with me.”

 

Chapter 16: Perplexed

Chapter Notes

To all the people on twt who asked for angst, here you go. To the person who said on ngl that Agatha “has had such a hard life and is not used to this much care” - you got me thinking. A lot. So maybe you are to blame for this.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

 

“Rio…” Agatha hesitates, her hands coming up to rest on Rio’s wrists where they cradle her face. 

“Agatha, move in with me.” Rio says again, her voice steady and sure. She leans down to kiss Agatha softly, but she feels Agatha stiffen beneath her lips. 

“You don’t know what you are asking,” she whispers. 

“Yes I do,” Rio insists. “I come home from work and you are there. We have dinner together. We go to bed together. We buy stupid little pumpkins on Halloween and get a tiny tree for Christmas.”

Agatha blinks hard. Rio can see the tears brimming along the edges of her eyes, threatening to fall. She can’t tell if they are out of joy and pain.

“Can we just talk about this later?” Her voice is small. 

“We can just talk about this now.”

“I can’t.” The words rip out of her. “Just…I have patients to see. It’s been a long morning already.” Agatha’s hands slip from Rio’s wrists. She takes a step back, then another, eyes flicking everywhere but Rio’s face. 

“That’s a lot of excuses.”

“I know,” Agatha starts backing up toward the hospital door as she speaks.“We’ll just…let’s talk later ok?” Agatha offers her a small smile. But it’s too thin and it doesn’t quite reach her eyes. 

“Agatha,” her words come out somewhere between a plea and a warning. 

“I’ll be around,” Agatha blurts, too fast, the words tumbling out like she’s hardly thinking about them. 

Then she turns and bolts for the hospital door. The glass catches a flash of her reflection before it swings shut, sealing her away. 

Rio doesn’t move. She swears her feet are molded into the cement beneath her because they suddenly feel so heavy that she can’t lift them.

She can barely fathom what just happened. Agatha was in her bed just this morning. Her mouth was on her last night. They were happy and content living in the bubble of her house. Agatha said she was willing to go to war for her - and she did. What the hell just changed?

She wants to fold into herself. Right here. In the middle of the damn hospital courtyard.

But she has to go about her day. She doesn’t have a choice. She just fought tooth and nail for her job - her job that now feels hollow, stupid without Agatha. She wants to just turn around, walk into the parking lot, get in her car and never look back. 

And she could.

What does she have tying her here? 

Two days ago, she knew what it was. Agatha. 

Agatha, who just walked away from her the second she got to close.

Before she realizes it, her feet are moving - carrying her across the sidewalk, through the parking lot to her car. Her hand closes around her door handle before her brain catches up. 

She loves her. 

She really fucking loves her.

And she knows…okay, she thinks…that under all her fear, Agatha loves her too. 

She’s not about to let that go without a fight. 

Maybe it is sheer delusion driving those thoughts.

She tells herself Agatha chose her. So much so that she was injured by her mother. So much so that she called off the wedding.

She did, didn’t she? 

It feels like Rio found a loose thread she can’t stop pulling - with every tug, something inside her unravels. 

Her pager sounds loudly in her pocket, bringing her back down to earth. 

Fuck. She has a list of patients. All sitting there in the hospital, waiting to be seen.

She swallows the small amount of bile bubbling up in the throat and crosses the parking lot again. Back to her job.

—

Rio feels like a robot.

Every patient gets reduced to a list - complaint, diagnostics, diagnosis, treatment. She’s the kind of doctor she would hate - blunt but efficient, in and out of the room in minutes. She leaves the nurses to console the family members, and the social worker to deal with the aftermath. She charts on autopilot. 

It’s nearly two hours before she spots her. 

Agatha is at a nurses’ station, huddled close to Jen. They are bent over a monitor, printing an EKG strip before sitting down to analyze it. 

Agatha looks…fine. 

She doesn’t look like she just put her entire heart on the line this morning. Then ripped Rio’s right out of her chest and stomped on it. 

She reaches into her white coat pocket, pulls out a pair of calipers, starting to measure the intervals on the strip. 

She focuses on analyzing it, her brow furrowed.

Then something shifts. 

Her gaze flickers, just for a second, but Rio catches it. Agatha’s eyes drift to the floor, unfocused. They seem to gloss over, like a memory playing back before her eyes. 

The calipers fall softly from her hand onto the table. Her hand rises almost absently, brushing her lips.  

For a moment, she looks…sad. 

And then it’s gone. She straightens, shakes her head as if physically forcing the thought away, and goes back to the EKG. 

Rio stands at the other end of the hall, half-hidden by her laptop screen resting on the desk. But her eyes never leave Agatha. 

She tells herself to keep working and stop looking. But her body won’t listen. It’s like watching a car crash in slow motion - Agatha rises from the desk, folding the EKG and shoving it into her coat pocket. Her hands stay buried there. She starts making her way down the hall, toward Rio, her eyes focused downward on her shoes. 

Rio’s breath catches when she realizes the path leads straight toward her. 

Suddenly, Agatha looks up, and she sees her. 

They make eye contact. 

Rio’s chest feels too tight, her pulse thudding behind her ribs. 

Agatha freezes mid-step, her lips parting just slightly, like she wants to say something - anything. 

But nothing comes. 

Instead, she turns sharply on her heel, almost colliding with a passing nurse. She mutters a quick apology as she heads in the other direction. Her pace quickens - first brisk, then urgent until she’s nearly running.

And just like that, she’s gone again. 

–

Rio finishes her day way earlier than she ever did when she had interns. No bedside rounding, no teaching, no charts to sign. Just silence.

It’s only early evening but Rio doesn’t want to go home yet. Not when it’s going to be so quiet there, the scent of Agatha still lingering in the air. Her toothbrush still sits on the counter, her oatmilk in the fridge, some overly priced shampoo in the shower. 

Rio knows she won’t move any of it. A tiny shrine to Agatha like she might come home one day. 

She realizes how pathetic it seems. But still, she grabs dinner from the cafeteria, packing it into a to-go container before taking the elevator to the fifth floor. She then takes the stairs up to the sixth. 

The abandoned equipment floor looks almost identical to how they left it weeks ago, apart from a few additional discharged boxes and one more broken hospital bed. 

She pushes a wobbly bed over near the window, angling it just enough to see the last bits of the sunset over the parking lot. 

She’s not two bites into her food when she hears footsteps behind her, coming toward her. They stop abruptly, pause for a second then seem to retreat. 

“You can’t avoid me forever,” Rio says without turning around. 

She’s met with only silence. For a moment, she thinks she imagined it. 

“I’m not avoiding you,” comes Agatha’s voice behind her, low and careful. 

Rio huffs. “You literally ran the other way when you saw me in the hall today.”

“I had remembered something I needed to do for a patient.”

“You know,” Rio says, turning her head slightly. “Others might think you are a great liar, but I watch you, Agatha. I see right through you. What are you doing here?” 

Agatha’s reply is small. “I needed some quiet.” 

Rio’s mouth curves, not quite a smile, but more a bitter smirk. “Realized you have no place to go after work?”

Agatha stiffens. “Don’t do that to me. Don’t try to hurt me just because I hurt you.” 

Now Rio finally turns to face her fully, dangling her legs off the edge of the bed.

She looks less put together than she expected, like the hardened shell of confidence has tiny cracks in it. Tendrils of hair fall from her ponytail, framing her face. She looks exhausted. 

“Are you going to finally talk to me then?” Rio asks.

Agatha shakes her head, blinking too fast. “You think this is easy for me?”

“No,” Rio says. “That’s the problem, I think you are making it harder than it needs to be.” 

Agatha lets out a disbelieving scoff, but she moves anyway, closing the space between them. She stops directly in front of where Rio sits on the bed.

Rio’s legs fall open instinctively, a silent invitation. Agatha steps in, close enough that Rio’s knees brush her thighs. They stay like that, like they are savoring some quiet moment of peace. 

Rio’s hand comes up to brush her knuckles along Agatha’s cheek. Her skin is warm where Agatha leans into her touch. 

In a last ditch effort, she decides to just admit it all. Rip her own heart out and offer it to Agatha. “I think I’m…I’m falling…”

“Don’t.” Agatha cuts her off. It’s too much. I can’t…” Agatha whispers. She turns her head, her cheek dragging against Rio’s hand as she pulls away. 

Rio furrows her brow, her voice fragile. “Then what did you mean in there, Agatha?” 

“I meant what I said,” Agatha swallows hard. “You’ve been my constant support. And…” 

“And?”

“Those feelings are real Rio. I just…I don’t know what they mean yet.”

“They don’t have to mean anything. They can just mean us. Being together.”

“I want to, don’t get me wrong.” Agatha says, her voice rushed. “But this…the injury, the suspension, me staying with you, the committee. It’s just a lot,” her voice falters, “It’s just a lot, really fast.” 

“What are you saying?” Rio shakes her head like she’s refusing to hear it. “Agatha, don’t do this to me….” 

She swears the world starts spinning around her because there is no other explanation for this. She can see the writing on the wall. And she can feel it too. Not just emotionally. Agatha is physically stepping backwards from her, shoulder curling inward, retreating inch by inch. 

“Maybe we should just take some time. To just think.” 

“Agatha, please,” Rio pleads. “Look how far we’ve come already. Look at everything we’ve sacrificed.” 

“That’s what I’m saying, Rio.” Her voice cracks, giving way to more frustration. “We keep giving little pieces of ourselves and our jobs away to make this work. At what point is it just too hard? It shouldn’t be this hard.” 

“You’re just scared.”

Agatha just huffs in response. “Scared? Look at what you are asking of me. I’ve been a doctor for six months. Six.” 

“No one in the history of this residency has had special treatment like you.” 

“Is that supposed to make me feel better?” Agatha’s tone rises now, her words sharper. 

“You asked me if it was worth it,” Rio says, her voice strained, edging on frustration. “I told you it was.” 

“But you didn’t ask me. What about me, Rio?” Rio opens her mouth to respond, but Agatha barrels on. “Have you thought at all about how this affects me? I’ve been living under my mother’s roof my entire life. My life that has been planned out for me. I don’t even know how to be on my own.” 

Agatha laughs now, something hollow, almost delirious. “I’ve been hiding everything for years. And now what? I’m supposed to tell everyone that I left my fiancé to shack up with my attending who is double my age?” 

Rio doesn’t have a response. The words just hang there, out in the open - because they’re true. 

Finally, Agatha breaks the silence. “Can you please just give me time?”

Rio’s throat tightens. “How much time, Agatha?”

“I don’t know.” 

Rio stares at the ground. She can’t look at her in the next moments because she knows what’s coming next and she doesn’t want to watch. 

“Don’t follow me, Rio.” 

Agatha looks at her one last time, eyes glassy, then turns away. It’s not until the sound of her footsteps fade down the hall, that Rio finally looks up. 

She just sits there for a long time, staring at the doorway like if she waits long enough, Agatha might walk back through it. 

But she doesn’t. 

The sunset has died outside the window by the time she stands, her dinner long since untouched. She drags her hand through her hair, swallowing hard against the lump rising in her throat. 

The ache sits too deep to cry, too raw to be angry. It’s just there. 

 — 

Rio calls Natasha before she even makes it out of the hospital. 

“This about the committee?” Natasha answers as soon as it rings.

“Worse.”

“Bar?” She questions and Rio can already hear her picking up her keys in the background.

“I’ll meet you there.”

Rio doesn’t bother changing out of her scrubs. She just drives. Her fingers ache from how hard she grips the steering wheel, eyes burning the whole way there. She tries not to think about the course of the entire day. How it started so well, Agatha in her passenger’s seat, her fingers brushing along her thigh as she drove. How she was her quiet strength as they drove into the parking lot. How she kissed her quickly before getting out of the car, reassuring her it would all be okay. 

And now, hours later, she’s alone, her chest feeling hollow, her brain numb from all the words they threw at each other. It feels impossible that it’s over, but it makes sense all the same. They were two sparks on dry kindling, the resulting fire growing wildly out of control in an instant. 

She beats Natasha there by a few minutes and sinks into a corner stool, away from everyone. 

When Natasha finally slides onto the stool beside her, she takes one look at Rio’s face and sighs. “Oh, sweetheart.” 

Natasha orders them both whiskey, but as Rio’s sits in front of her, she just stares at the amber liquid. She takes a long inhale, then starts telling Natasha everything. From the beginning - the call room, the sneaking around, even Agatha’s drunken night. It all comes barreling forward, tumbling out of her mouth like word vomit. 

“Sounds like you two are toxic together,” Natasha says finally. 

When Rio laughs, it’s hollow and cold. “We’re not.” But she’s not sure she believes her own words. 

“You’re toxically obsessed with each other,” Natasha counters. “To the point where neither of you can function.” 

“She’s not obsessed with me.” Rio takes a long sip of her drink. 

“You sure?” Natasha’s tone is gentle. 

Rio swallows. “She said it was moving too fast. That she wanted space. Doesn’t even sound like she wants me.” 

“Or,” Natasha says, leaning closer. “She’s so obsessed it scares her. So she runs. See? Toxic. Both of you.” 

“So what?” Rio murmurs. “It’s never going to work? Is that what you’re saying?” She downs the rest of her drink in one gulp. The liquor burns all the way down, her eyes stinging as it hits. 

Natasha shakes her head. “No. It could work. But you both have to stop hurting each other just to feel close to each other.”

Rio stares down at her now empty drink. “I’ve tried. It’s like none of it matters.”

“Have you really, though?” 

Maybe it’s the alcohol, too much too fast, or maybe it’s the quiet ache that’s been building all night - but Rio’s hand moves before she can think. She runs her fingers along Natasha’s arm, nails dragging lightly against her skin.

She can forget her. Fill the voice with someone else. Another body. It could work. She just has to get the never ending picture of Agatha out of her head. Somehow. 

“Like old times?” Her fingers lock around Natasha’s wrist, tugging her slightly closer to her along the bar top. 

For a heartbeat, Natasha leans in. Her eyes flicker, half-lidded. Then she lets out a long, tired sigh. 

“You don’t want this distraction, Rio.” Natasha pulls her arm away. “Not me. Not tonight. You want her. And the only way you’ll get her back is if she wants to come back.”

Rio can feel the tears prickling the back of her eyes, part shame, part sadness. “And if she doesn’t?”

“Then it wasn’t meant to be.” 

Rio nods, but its hollow. It’s everything and nothing she wanted to hear. 

—

Every day is torture. 

Okay maybe torture is a bit dramatic. But every day still sucks ass.

Because every single day, Rio now has to step foot in the hospital alone. Everyday she sees the call room where they slept together, the hallways where they shared secret kisses, the conference room where Agatha defended her. Everyday she eats lunch on the damn equipment floor where Agatha asked for more time. 

Time.

Such a vague term.

How much time is enough? Does Rio wave in the hallway, pretend it’s normal, hoping that one day Agatha turns around and says she’s ready?

Does she attempt to move on - knowing full well she can’t? Is she allowed to ask how long she’s supposed to wait before this silence means it’s really over?

The whole thing is bullshit. And a little elementary. 

But what’s that saying “if you love something let it go; if it comes back, it’s yours?”

Also bullshit. 

Work at least keeps her moving, even if it’s slowly crushing her. The hospital is drowning in flu admissions, overloading Rio (and everyone else’s) caseload. Rio swears months go by, but when she looks at the calendar, it’s only been a few weeks. 

Today at least she has something different. Worse but different. 

A woman, in her 40’s, Rio’s age. Except she came into the emergency room with stomach pain one day and walked out with a stage 4 cancer diagnosis. 

Both her and her husband want to fight it - doing anything and everything. Rio connects with her instantly, promising to work as hard as she can to get her treatment. 

Then things spiral. She has a reaction to the first chemotherapy, and has a gene mutation that means the second one won’t work. 

Oncology has said she needs experimental chemotherapy. She’s exhausted all other options. 

And of course - the drugs aren’t FDA-approved for her condition. And expensive as hell. 

“Shit!” Rio slams her fist into the counter next to her. She’s claimed one of the oncology wing desks, surrounded by stacks of grant applications, research papers and pharmaceutical trial lists - every possible avenue. All of them dead ends. 

“You okay over there?” The voice to her right makes her jump. 

“I’m fine, Agatha,” she grates without looking up. 

It’s like this most days. She can’t completely avoid Agatha. They see each other in the conference rooms, pass near each other in hallways, glance awkwardly at each other during lunches. 

There is usually a courteous “hi” or “how are you,” before they both retreat back behind their professional walls. 

Nothing more. 

They never linger. Never touch. 

Occasionally Billy is nearby muttering about how ridiculous they are both being. 

Today something changes. 

Rio can feel Agatha rise from her chair beside her, the faint shuffle of her feet moving closer. 

Rio doesn’t move, she keeps her eyes straight ahead, glued to the papers in front of her. 

Agatha steps in behind her, close enough that Rio can feel the warmth of her body at her back. She leans over, peering at the research papers spread across the desk. 

“You’re trying to get Blincyto for a patient?” Agatha’s voice is soft, curious. 

“Yes?” Rio replies, her voice clipped. 

“It’s like $70,000 a month.”

“I’m aware. But my patient doesn’t have any other options.”

“And insurance denied it?” Agatha asks. 

“Of course,” Rio murmurs. 

Agatha folds her arms, thinking. “Then appeal to Evanora. The hospital has charitable funds set aside for cases like this. It would make them look good.” 

Rio lets out a dry laugh. “Ha! Like she’d approve of that coming from me.” 

“You never know.” Agatha shrugs. “This is professional, not personal.”

Rio glances sideways, lips curling. “What, do you have a soft spot for her now?”

Agatha doesn’t bite. She simply ignores her, stepping backward and straightening. 

Then as if nothing happened, she asks, “Are you coming to the gala tonight?”

“That stupid hospital fundraiser?”

Agatha nods once. “Pretty sure everyone’s expected to go.” 

Rio sticks her tongue in her cheek. “Are you going?” She tries not to sound too hopeful, and fails.

Agatha hesitates, just long enough for Rio to notice. “Yeah,” she says finally, meeting her eyes. “I’ll be there.” Her words are soft, almost tentative. Or maybe Rio is just imagining it. She doesn’t know anymore, and part of her doesn’t care. If she can only see Agatha in passing like this, small crumbs of pleasantries, she’ll take it.

“I guess I will to then.” Rio swallows hard. 

Agatha presses her lips together, nodding, then turns to walk away. A few steps later, she stops, turning toward Rio. “I’ll see you there then.” 

Rio turns back to her papers, a faint blush across her cheeks. 

— 

 

Chapter End Notes

Please don't throw tomatoes

Chapter 17: Quit

Chapter Notes

Alexa play: imgonnagetyouback by Taylor swift

 

The gala is every bit as ridiculous as Rio expected it to be. 

The hospital has taken over a downtown conference center, the beige wells she remembers have vanished beneath layers of white linen. The tables are covered in oversized flower arrangements and fine china. Waiters roam between tables with trays of champagne and appetizers. 

Local big wigs and business owners mingle with the hospital higher ups - everyone kissing everyone’s ass in hopes of more money. 

Apart from the ridiculous $500 a head ticket cost (that every doctor was “voluntold” to pay), Rio isn’t sure how this event  is supposed to raise money and not spend it. 

Luckily, Rio had a few dresses in the back of her closet for occasions such as this. Tonight she opted for a red dress - one with a long cut out of her stomach and a way too high slit up her thigh. It isn’t subtle. But she didn’t want to be. If anything, she wants her dress to scream “why don’t you want me” right to Agatha’s face. 

By the head turns she gets from a few men as she walks in, and one sneer from a wife, it might be working. 

She weaves her way into the already crowded space and immediately beelines it for the bar. Better to face a night like this slightly tipsy. The bar is crowded with faces she doesn’t recognize and a few she’s seen roaming the hospital hallways. She gives a few courtesy nods but avoids talking to anyone. After paying for a drink (it’s not even an open bar), she starts searching for her table number. 

She easily spots Jen where she is chatting nearby with Alice, her fingers hovering too closely to her lower back. Rio narrows her eyes at the pair. They are too happy, too carefree, even at a work event. It seems unfair. Jen catches the look and quickly drops her hand, forcing a bright smile as she waves her over. 

Rio returns a tight-lipped smile in reply and gestures toward the tables, pretending she’s busy. 

Her gaze drifts across the glittering crowd as if she’s simply taking in the spectacle. But there’s only one person she’s really looking for. 

She scans the room once, trying hard to spot her unruly hair. Nothing.

She scans the faces again quickly, a slight panic flashing over her eyes. No sign of her. She swears she said she was going to be here. A small lump of disappointment settles low in her chest. 

Instead, her eyes find the one person she wishes she hadn’t. 

Evanora.

She stands near the front, flanked by a circle of men in dark suits who laugh too loudly at everything she says. Her power suit, although tailored, still appears a size too big for her small frame. Unfortunately, the bruise Rio left her has since faded. 

Rio threads her way through the crowd, dodging a few greetings and a waiter balancing a tray of crab cakes. Another passes by with champagne and she snags two flutes without breaking her stride. 

Evanora’s voice carries easily above the hum of conversation - Rio can hear her saying something about the hospital’s “record breaking quarter,” due to her "efficiency” and “budgeting.” The men chuckle obligingly as she jokes the nurses don’t seem to mind the pay cut, or the extra shifts. 

Rio slips into the small circle beside her, fitting neatly into the empty space between Evanora and a red-face executive. She plasters on her best fake smile.
